- 2026-07-05 provider DAG failure-classification hardening: the broad provider-live regression found two defects after `herdr pane run` prompt submission was fixed. First, provider reviewer prompts allowed subagents to compute a raw `sha256sum` of the work-order file instead of copying the canonical `work_order_sha256` field, which caused max-attempt exhaustion to be reported as `REVIEWER_RECEIPT_INVALID` instead of the intended `REVISE` fail-closed verdict. Second, an invalid reviewer model caused the reviewer worker pane to disappear without a receipt, but Tau classified the result as a generic `REVIEWER_RECEIPT_TIMEOUT`. `src/tau_coding/provider_dag_poc.py` now tells coder/reviewer nodes to copy the embedded work-order hash, probes started reviewer worker panes, and, on missing receipt, checks whether the worker pane exited so the alert becomes `reviewer_send_failed` with a `provider_worker_exited_before_receipt` evidence line and a goal-guardian reroute recommendation. `scripts/run-real-world-sanity.py` now expects the invalid-model fail-closed lane to return `REVIEWER_SEND_FAILED`. Focused proof: `uv run ruff check --select I,F src/tau_coding/provider_dag_poc.py tests/test_provider_pane_poc.py scripts/run-real-world-sanity.py` -> pass; `uv run pytest tests/test_provider_pane_poc.py tests/test_real_world_sanity_runner.py -q` -> `41 passed in 2.67s`. Targeted provider-live proof: `scripts/run-real-world-sanity.py --levels advanced --checks advanced.provider_dag_max_attempts_fail_closed,advanced.provider_dag_invalid_model_fail_closed --label tau-provider-failure-classification-fix2-20260705 --receipt-timeout-seconds 300 --provider-cleanup-mode apply` exited 0. Receipt `experiments/goal-locked-subagents/proofs/real-world-sanity/20260705T204602Z-tau-provider-failure-classification-fix2-20260705/real-world-sanity-receipt.json` reports `status:"PASS"`, `mocked:false`, `live:"mixed"`, `provider_live:true`, `check_count:2`, and `failed_check_count:0`; max-attempts reports nested `status:"BLOCKED"` / `verdict:"REVISE"` after two attempts, and invalid-model reports nested `status:"BLOCKED"` / `verdict:"REVIEWER_SEND_FAILED"` with `alert_codes:["reviewer_send_failed"]`. Broad provider-live proof: `scripts/run-real-world-sanity.py --levels advanced --checks advanced.generic_provider_dag_adapter,advanced.generic_provider_dag_adapter_resume,advanced.provider_dag_repair_loop,advanced.provider_dag_max_attempts_fail_closed,advanced.provider_dag_invalid_model_fail_closed --label tau-provider-broad-failure-classification-fix-20260705 --receipt-timeout-seconds 300 --provider-cleanup-mode apply` exited 0. - 2026-07-05 Herdr session ownership cleanup slice: `src/tau_coding/herdr_cleanup.py` now supports explicit `tau.herdr_session_ownership.v1` input for run-owned Herdr session cleanup. `tau herdr-cleanup apply` still blocks recorded session candidates without `--session-ownership`, but with a matching unexpired ownership artifact it runs `herdr session stop <session>`, verifies absence with `herdr session get <session>` expecting `session_not_found`, then closes and verifies the run-owned workspace. `src/tau_coding/cli.py` adds `--session-ownership <ownership.json>`, and `src/tau_coding/run_status.py` now exposes cleanup `workspace_lease`, `session_ownership`, alert count, applied session-stop count, applied workspace-close count, and post-verified absence count. - 2026-07-05 command-spec trust policy hardening slice: `src/tau_coding/handoff_dispatch.py` now treats command-spec intent fields `requires_network`, `mutates`, and `requires_clean_worktree` as executable policy gates. A command spec that requests network access is rejected unless `tau.command_spec_policy.v1.allows_network:true`; a mutating command spec is rejected unless `allows_mutation:true`; and specs or policies that require a clean worktree run `git status --porcelain` and fail closed on dirty or non-readable repositories. Focused proof: `uv run ruff check --select I,F,E501 src/tau_coding/handoff_dispatch.py tests/test_handoff_dispatch.py` -> pass; `uv run pytest tests/test_handoff_dispatch.py tests/test_project_dag.py -q` -> `57 passed`; `git diff --check -- src/tau_coding/handoff_dispatch.py tests/test_handoff_dispatch.py` -> pass. This proves command-backed handoff and project-DAG command-spec dispatch now fail closed for disallowed network, mutation, denied commands, cwd escapes, and dirty-worktree requirements before subagent execution. It does not prove every existing command spec declares perfect intent, provider/model semantic quality, GitHub mutation approval, or production repository mutation.
- 2026-07-05 evidence manifest hardening slice: `src/tau_coding/evidence_manifest.py` now binds JSON evidence items with declared schemas to the manifest `goal_hash` and rejects declared validators that do not use the `tau evidence-validate ...` namespace. This closes a typed-evidence gap where an artifact could match its schema/hash while carrying a different immutable goal hash, or where a manifest could mark evidence as `valid:true` under a non-Tau validator string. Focused proof: `uv run ruff check --select I,F,E501 src/tau_coding/evidence_manifest.py tests/test_evidence_manifest.py` -> pass; `uv run pytest tests/test_evidence_manifest.py tests/test_project_dag.py -q` -> `34 passed`; `git diff --check -- src/tau_coding/evidence_manifest.py tests/test_evidence_manifest.py` -> pass. This proves local deterministic evidence-manifest validation now fails closed for schema/hash mismatches, goal-hash mismatches, and non-Tau validator declarations before DAG dispatch consumes the manifest. It does not prove semantic correctness of artifact contents beyond declared schema/hash/goal checks, provider/model quality, or GitHub/Memory/browser side effects.

- 2026-07-04 Operational lesson for Tau adaptive DAG work: do not stop at a `Remaining non-claims` list when the remaining item is an implemented branch that can be deterministically exercised. Convert it into the next proof command or explicitly ask for the required side-effect target before ending the turn. For side-effecting proof such as Memory `/upsert`, state the target collection before executing and preserve an audit receipt plus readback artifact.

Nested cleanup receipt `.../provider-runs/20260703T222858Z-rw-sanity-generic-provider-dag-adapter/herdr-cleanup-receipt.json` reports `schema:"tau.herdr_cleanup_receipt.v1"`, `status:"PASS"`, `ok:true`, `mocked:false`, `live:true`, `mode:"apply"`, `candidate_count:1`, `applied_actions[0].workspace_id:"w2Q"`, `applied:true`, and `returncode:0`; direct post-condition `herdr workspace get w2Q` returned `workspace_not_found` with exit code `1`. `uv run tau run-status .../advanced-generic-provider-dag-adapter` reports `detected_type:"generic_dag"`, `status:"PASS"`, `resumed_node_count:1`, node `provider_live:true`, and artifact map pointing to the nested cleanup/evidence receipts. This proves Tau can resume a provider-backed generic DAG node from receipts after the live provider workspace has already been closed by scoped cleanup; it does not prove Herdr pane reattachment after process restart, provider-native session.ready events, production mutation, ticket closure, remote Tailscale monitoring, browser/CDP UI rendering, global cleanup, Git worktree deletion, or session deletion.

- 2026-07-03 Provider-backed generic DAG resume now has live proof and the adapter signs work-order receipts. - 2026-07-03 Generic DAG resume now guards against stale work-order receipts. `src/tau_coding/generic_dag.py` computes `work_order_sha256` for nodes with `work_order_path`, requires node receipts to match that current hash, records the hash in node records, and exposes `work_order_path` / `work_order_sha256` through `tau dag-inspect`; stale or unreadable work-order receipts are not treated as valid resume checkpoints. `tests/test_generic_dag.py` covers matching work-order receipts and stale receipt non-resume behavior. `scripts/run-real-world-sanity.py` adds `medium.generic_dag_stale_work_order_blocks`, which prewrites a valid-looking planner receipt for an old work-order hash, mutates the work order, then verifies `tau dag-run` does not resume the stale receipt and blocks when the rerun command fails. Docs updated in `docs/generic-dag-runner.md` and `docs/real-world-sanity-checks.md`. - 2026-06-29 Tau now has an explicit built-in self-fix requirement in the README and configuration docs. Self-fix means a background cron/watchdog can read eligible `grahama1970/tau` issues, acquire a lease, run Memory `/intent` and `/recall` before code inspection, validate a goal-helper packet, dispatch coder and reviewer through the Tau harness with Scillm as the LLM caller, loop until reviewer PASS/BLOCKED/retry exhaustion, then post receipts/comments/labels and update project knowledge. Eligibility must be explicit via trusted labels or comments such as `agent-work`, `agent:coder`, `tau-harness`, `route:backend_python_or_skill_runtime`, or a future `/tau self-fix` command. Self-fix must create a pre-fix git checkpoint before mutation and revert Tau's own failed fix if proof fails or reviewer finds a regression, preserving unrelated human changes and stopping before mutation when human changes cannot be isolated. Human-only gates still apply for immutable goal changes, scope expansion, destructive operations, releases, and final acceptance.
- 2026-06-29 Tau now has an explicit README/configuration requirement that goal-helper behavior is built into the orchestrated harness as a hard-stop control. Long-running loops, cron-dispatched issues, repeated repair attempts, and live Tau/Memory/browser/harness/subagent/GitHub/compliance/runtime proofs must have a proof-driven goal packet with primary live proof, completion criteria, allowed scope, forbidden drift, retry budget, stop condition, and escalation bundle. Hard-stop escalation is Memory-first: write the help bundle, call Memory `/intent`, use `/recall`, `/clarify`, or `/deflect` according to the product, and only call external research when Memory routes to research. The human-selected research service belongs in `~/.tau/research.json` and may be WebGPT, a configured LLM provider/model, Brave Search for external docs, or manual-human. Every Tau session that touches loop, harness, TUI, chat, Memory routing, GitHub orchestration, or subagent behavior must end with a `PROJECT_KNOWLEDGE.md` update and Memory sync or an explicit sync blocker.

- Project initialized, knowledge tracking started
- Tâ€™au is a fork of alejandro-ao/tau being hardened into a goal-locked agentic harness. Current local slices add Loop2-compatible run receipts plus minimal model-facing contracts for subagent receipts, generated tickets, handoffs, and human-only goal changes. Tâ€™au derives GitHub labels deterministically instead of asking model agents to duplicate label/projection fields.
- The human-facing README now follows the `watch` skill README pattern: compressed banner image first, short promise, practical "what it does", "when to use it", quickstart, current direction, repository map, and evidence discipline. The header image is stored as `docs/assets/tau-header.webp`, compressed with Pillow from the provided PNG.
- Tâ€™au's current product direction is Memory-first shared chat plus a goal-locked harness. The chat enters through Memory intent/extract/recall before answer, clarify, deflect, research, or compliance behavior. Subagent routing and GitHub ticket projection must remain receipt-backed and fail-closed.
- Tâ€™au now has a repo-owned chat UX contract at `ui/tau-chat-contract.json`. UX Lab's `#tau` route should act as an integration viewer for that contract, similar to Watch, rather than being treated as the canonical owner of the Tâ€™au chat UX.
- README now explicitly separates the loop, harness, TUI, and chat surfaces. The loop is bounded; the harness validates receipts and routing; the TUI is the terminal renderer; the chat is the Watch-style human inspection surface for Memory stages, handoff JSON, dry-run GitHub projection, and proof boundaries.
- README now documents the main fork delta from upstream Tau: Loop2 receipts, minimal JSON contracts, human goal-change bridge, goal-guardian reconciliation, command-backed subagent dispatch, GitHub transport, read-only ticket-source fetch, Memory-first chat routes, external receipt intake, dry-run external GitHub projection, and the Tâ€™au-owned UX contract.

- 2026-06-28 Memory route adapter hardening now validates first-class Memory products before accepting successful HTTP JSON. `memory.answer` requires `schema=memory.answer.v1` and boolean `can_answer`; `memory.clarify` requires `schema=memory.clarify.v1` and boolean `needs_clarification`; `memory.deflect` requires `schema=memory.deflect.v1` and boolean `should_deflect`; malformed Brave JSON for RESEARCH fails closed instead of throwing. This still does not prove final Sparta Chat readiness, semantic correctness of the compliance answer, unbounded autonomous subagent operation, live Brave execution, or human acceptance of the terminal human route.
- 2026-06-28 Memory ANSWER route selection now respects the first-class `/intent` product before entity-clarification fallback. If Memory returns `action=ANSWER` with sufficient confidence, the experiment-local selector chooses `memory.answer` and records reason `memory_intent_answer` instead of downgrading to `memory.clarify` only because the entity packet is empty. Focused command `uv run pytest experiments/loop2-alignment/reliability-stress/test_memory_brave_harness.py tests/test_live_memory_chat_command_loop_proofs.py -q` passed 44 tests. This is a deterministic selector regression proof; it still does not prove a live browser prompt that naturally causes `/api/memory/intent` to select ANSWER.
- 2026-06-28 Fresh multi-step non-human command-loop proof is captured in `experiments/goal-locked-subagents/proofs/fresh-multistep-command-loop-20260628T150848Z/manifest.json`. `uv run tau handoff-command-loop --max-steps 4` consumed a `tau.agent_handoff.v1` start packet, selected `goal-guardian` then `project-or-harness-verifier`, recorded command exits `[0,0]`, preserved the active goal hash through goal-guardian, and stopped at terminal `human` with `mocked:false`, `live:true`, `step_count:2`, and `stop_reason=next_agent_is_human`. This proves a fresh bounded two-subagent local command loop; it does not prove unbounded autonomous operation, fresh live GitHub mutation for this specific run, final Sparta Chat readiness, or semantic Memory answer correctness.
- 2026-06-28 Special-mode start handoff hardening now has focused regressions for stale goal hashes before dispatch. `run_agent_handoff_command_loop` blocks a stale start handoff at step 1 with `stop_reason=invalid_handoff`, zero dispatches, and no selected command execution; `write_agent_handoff_command_loop_receipt` writes the same fail-closed `command-loop-receipt.json` with empty dispatch/artifact lists. Focused command `uv run pytest tests/test_handoff_dispatch.py -q` passed 19 tests; broader contract command `uv run pytest tests/test_handoff_dispatch.py tests/test_generated_ticket.py tests/test_cli.py -q` passed 147 tests.
- 2026-06-28 Tau cron special-mode preflight now fails closed before scheduling ticks when `TAU_ORCHESTRATOR_START` is missing or does not point to a mounted file. `docker/tau-cron.sh` writes `tau.cron_preflight_receipt.v1` under `TAU_RECEIPT_DIR`, records `command_executed:false`, `mocked:false`, `live:true`, and exits before `handoff-command-loop` can run. Focused command `uv run pytest tests/test_tau_cron.py -q` passed 2 tests; adjacent contract command `uv run pytest tests/test_tau_cron.py tests/test_handoff_dispatch.py tests/test_generated_ticket.py tests/test_cli.py -q` passed 149 tests.
- 2026-06-28 Tau cron now supports deterministic one-tick execution with `TAU_ORCHESTRATOR_ONCE=1`, so a mounted valid start handoff can be smoke-tested without launching an endless scheduler. `tests/test_tau_cron.py` proves the script invokes exactly one `tau handoff-command-loop` with `--start`, `--receipt-dir`, `--agents-root`, `--command-spec-root`, `--active-goal-hash`, and `--goal-guardian-ticket-source`, then exits with code 0. Focused command `uv run pytest tests/test_tau_cron.py -q` passed 3 tests; adjacent contract command `uv run pytest tests/test_tau_cron.py tests/test_handoff_dispatch.py tests/test_generated_ticket.py tests/test_cli.py -q` passed 150 tests.
- 2026-06-28 Docker Compose one-tick smoke for the special orchestrated subagent mode produced `.tmp/docker-cron-smoke/receipts/20260628T012315Z/command-loop-receipt.json` with `schema=tau.agent_handoff_command_loop_receipt.v1`, `mocked:false`, `live:true`, `ok:true`, `status=WAITING`, `step_count:1`, `terminal_agent=human`, `stop_reason=next_agent_is_human`, `dispatches[0].selected_agent=reviewer`, and command exit `0`. The fixture is `experiments/goal-locked-subagents/fixtures/docker-cron-start-handoff.json`; the command-spec overlays now use container-portable `cwd:"."`.
- Tau now has a repo-local `Dockerfile`, `.dockerignore`, `docker-compose.yml`, and `docker/tau-cron.sh`. The compose stack owns Tau CLI and Tau cron containers while treating Memory, SciLLM, Brave Search, and UX Lab as explicit external services by URL or mounted skill path.
- Tau now has one-step dispatch receipts for routed handoffs. `handoff-dispatch-agent-command` validates the start handoff, selects `next_agent.name`, loads an opt-in `tau-dispatch-command.json` from that agent registry entry, runs one bounded command, and validates stdout as the next `tau.agent_handoff.v1`.
- Tau can now use a committed command-spec overlay with `--command-spec-root`. The selected agent is still validated against `/home/graham/workspace/experiments/agent-skills/agents`, but the executable `tau-dispatch-command.json` can live under Tau's `experiments/goal-locked-subagents/agent-command-specs/` tree for reproducible harness experiments.
- Built-in `goal-guardian` now has a deterministic adapter. It reads the start handoff from stdin, requires `TAU_HANDOFF_ACTIVE_GOAL_HASH`, refuses stale goal hashes, and emits a normal `tau.agent_handoff.v1` only when the active goal hash is preserved.
- Tau now has a command-backed local loop receipt. `handoff-command-loop` repeatedly validates the current handoff, loads the selected agent command spec, runs one bounded command, validates the emitted handoff, and stops at `human` or fails closed.
- Tau can render or explicitly apply GitHub transport for a command-loop terminal handoff. `handoff-command-loop-github-transport` extracts the last response projection from a successful command-loop receipt that stopped at `human`, renders the exact `gh issue/pr comment` and label-edit commands by default, and only runs them when `--apply` is passed.
- The command-loop GitHub apply path is fail-closed before mutation: invalid receipts return `ok: false`, `applied: false`, and zero command executions even when `--apply` is passed.
- Valid command-loop GitHub apply now runs live preflight checks before mutation: `gh auth status --hostname github.com` and `gh issue/pr view <number> --repo <repo> --json number`. If preflight fails, the receipt records `preflight_results`, leaves `command_results` empty, and returns `applied: false`.
- The experiment-local Memory/Brave harness now writes `stage_trace` and `current_stage` into `tau.loop2_memory_skill_selector_harness.v1` receipts so chat/TUI consumers can render dynamic Memory pipeline state from receipt data instead of static "thinking" text.
- UX Lab's Tau chat surface now renders a receipt-backed current-stage panel from the Memory stage-trace proof. The pi-mono commit is `225321964` on `persona/tim-blazytko-1774553751276`; the rendered `#tau` page shows `Receipt-backed current stage`, `Clarifying...`, and the stage-trace artifact path.
- UX Lab's Tau chat composer has live interaction proof for the Memory stage indicator. A real browser turn on `http://127.0.0.1:3002/#tau` submitted `How does Tau handle a CWE-287 SPARTA evidence case?`, observed `shared-chat:live-thinking-trace` with `Accessing Memory...`, recorded five `/api/memory/*` responses, and produced the final Memory-first contract fields.
- UX Lab's Tau chat adapter now fails closed when a selected Memory route endpoint does not return a route product. The pi-mono commit is `26dbf4917` on `persona/tim-blazytko-1774553751276`; focused tests cover CLARIFY, DEFLECT, ANSWER, RESEARCH, and COMPLIANCE route behavior plus no-handoff semantics for missing CLARIFY/DEFLECT/ANSWER products.
- UX Lab's Tau chat has live browser route evidence for CLARIFY, DEFLECT, RESEARCH, and COMPLIANCE through the real Memory proxy. `/api/memory/answer` is live and returned `memory.answer.v1` with `can_answer: true`, but current `/api/memory/intent` selected `QUERY` rather than `ANSWER` for the probed Tau answer prompt, so no browser ANSWER route was forced or mocked.
- UX Lab's Tau chat now renders the full `tau.agent_handoff.v1` JSON contract in successful route messages after the human-readable handoff and GitHub projection tables. The pi-mono commit is `57ddd5304` on `persona/tim-blazytko-1774553751276`; fail-closed route product failures still omit the handoff JSON.
- Tau now has a committed `reviewer` command-spec overlay that can consume the UI-rendered `tau.agent_handoff.v1` JSON route and emit one bounded reviewer response through `handoff-agent-adapter`. A live command-loop proof extracted the JSON from `http://127.0.0.1:3002/#tau`, selected `reviewer`, ran one command with exit `0`, and stopped at `human`.
- Command-loop terminal GitHub transport now supports `target: "new"` for UI-originated handoffs. The dry-run path renders `gh issue create` with the handoff body and derived labels instead of failing when the Tau chat handoff is not yet attached to an existing issue.
- Tau now has a trusted-human goal-change bridge. `human-goal-change-bridge` validates a `tau.human_goal_change.v1` packet, requires `--trusted-human` plus the current active goal hash, writes a `tau.human_goal_change_bridge_receipt.v1`, and writes a normal `tau.agent_handoff.v1` start handoff routed to `goal-guardian` only on success.
- The command-loop stop order now recognizes a response that routes to `human` on the final allowed step. Before this fix, a valid final-step human route could be mislabeled as `max_steps_exhausted`.
- Tau has a committed `.ask/browser-oracles.yaml` plus `.ask/README.md` for WebGPT escalation. Current Tau convention is direct `$webgpt` with project `tau`; `$ask` is reserved for later workflows that need its full review runtime.
- Goal-guardian now has a bounded reconciliation path for bridged human goal changes. If the incoming handoff contains `context.human_goal_change`, the adapter writes `tau.goal_guardian_reconciliation_receipt.v1`, records the proposed new goal, marks open-ticket reconciliation as not started without an authoritative ticket source, and routes to `human` before any non-human continuation.
- Goal-guardian reconciliation can now consume an authoritative local `tau.goal_guardian_ticket_source.v1` file via `TAU_GOAL_GUARDIAN_TICKET_SOURCE`. When present, the receipt classifies tickets into `keep`, `close`, `migrate`, and `regenerate` buckets and still routes to `human`.
- Tau can now render dry-run GitHub transport for a `tau.goal_guardian_reconciliation_receipt.v1`. `goal-guardian-reconciliation-github-transport` validates the receipt, embeds it in a GitHub comment body, derives `agent-work,next:human,executor:human,goal-change`, and remains apply-gated.
- Tau can now fetch a goal-guardian ticket source from GitHub Issues with `goal-guardian-ticket-source-github-fetch`. The default path is dry-run and only renders `gh issue list`; `--execute` runs the read-only issue-list command, writes `tau.goal_guardian_ticket_source.v1`, and fails closed without writing a source when GitHub rejects the request.
- `handoff-goal-guardian-adapter` now accepts `--ticket-source <path>` for explicit goal-change ticket reconciliation input. This keeps command specs and direct adapter runs from depending on hidden environment state; `TAU_GOAL_GUARDIAN_TICKET_SOURCE` remains a fallback.
- `handoff-command-loop` now accepts `--goal-guardian-ticket-source <path>`. When the selected agent is `goal-guardian` and its command spec invokes `handoff-goal-guardian-adapter`, Tau appends `--ticket-source <resolved path>` to the recorded command so the command-loop receipt names the exact ticket-source artifact used for reconciliation.
- `handoff-command-loop-reconciliation-github-transport` now starts from a command-loop receipt, extracts the goal-guardian reconciliation artifact, renders the dry-run GitHub comment/label commands, and writes a wrapper receipt that names the source loop receipt, reconciliation receipt, and ticket-source artifact.
- 2026-07-04 Evaluation note: a Herdr-backed reasoning-monitor feature is architecturally plausible for Tau only if it monitors observable traces and receipts, not private hidden chain-of-thought. Current Tau evidence supports receipt-level validation through tau.agent_handoff.v1, goal_hash/route/target checks, events.jsonl ledgers, provider readiness/Herdr pane receipts, run-status summaries, and steering/follow-up queues. The missing feature boundary is a thin integration layer that runs subagents in Herdr-managed panes or another streaming surface, requires structured trace JSONL before final handoff, and lets the monitor alert/reroute/fail-closed without mutating the immutable goal.
- 2026-07-04 Corrected feature framing: call the proposed feature a JSON trace / goal-alignment monitor, not a reasoning-trace evaluator. The monitor should evaluate observable declarations and artifacts only: intent summaries, structured plan/status events, tool calls, evidence_claim records, artifact writes, route state, draft handoffs, and final receipts. It must not depend on hidden chain-of-thought. Recommended separation: creator produces work/evidence/draft handoff; monitor emits tau.monitor_alert.v1 on goal drift, missing evidence, route discontinuity, unsafe scope expansion, or contradictory claims; orchestrator applies policy by steering, blocking, retrying, rerouting to goal-guardian, or escalating to human.
- 2026-07-04 Traycer monitor implementation decision: start with `tau traycer validate` as an offline JSONL invariant monitor before live Herdr streaming. The valuable primitive is the trace contract, not terminal scrollback. First slice should validate `tau.subagent_trace.v1`, `tau.evidence_claim.v1`, final `tau.agent_handoff.v1`, active goal hash, target continuity, required evidence, and scope/route invariants, then write `tau.monitor_receipt.v1` plus cited `tau.monitor_alert.v1` records with severities WARN, REVIEW, REROUTE, and BLOCK. Later rungs can add `tau traycer tail` for live JSONL tailing and `tau traycer herdr-watch` for Herdr pane transport/control. Monitor detects and recommends; orchestrator decides; goal-guardian reconciles drift; only the human may change the immutable goal.
- 2026-07-04 Monitor-to-handoff contract decision: keep `tau.agent_handoff.v1` compact. The handoff should reference monitor results rather than absorb full alert detail: include a `context.artifacts[]` monitor receipt reference with schema/path/sha256, a `result.evidence[]` monitor verdict/hash summary, and optionally a compact `monitor` summary object for routing. `tau.monitor_receipt.v1` is the authoritative audit artifact containing trace hash, final handoff hash, alert list, severity counts, verdict, and `does_not_prove`; `tau.monitor_alert.v1` rows are cited by id/hash in the handoff only when unresolved or severe. Routing rule: PASS routes normally, WARN routes normally with reviewer inspection required, REVIEW routes to reviewer or human, REROUTE routes to goal-guardian/reviewer/human, and BLOCK must produce a blocked handoff routed to goal-guardian or human rather than claiming completion.
- 2026-07-04 Traycer first-slice policy decisions: do not modify `tau.agent_handoff.v1` or add a top-level `monitor` field in slice one; use existing `context.artifacts[]` and `result.evidence[]` only. `tau traycer validate` strict mode should use authoritative required evidence from `--required-evidence` or `--start-handoff`; final handoff `required_evidence` is fallback/advisory only and must record `evidence_authority:"final_handoff_fallback"` plus an authority warning. Default severity semantics: WARN keeps `ok:true` and `status:"PASS"`; REVIEW uses `ok:false`, `status:"REVIEW"`, `next_allowed:false`, and `review_required:true`; REROUTE and BLOCK also set `ok:false`/`next_allowed:false`. `tau traycer validate` must remain pure: input trace plus handoff plus policy produces `tau.monitor_receipt.v1`; it should not rewrite handoffs or mutate route state. BLOCK receipts include a `recommended_action` such as reroute to `goal-guardian`, while the orchestrator owns any blocked-handoff projection.
- 2026-07-04 Traycer DAG drift decision: DAG drift should be checked as a second layer above per-subagent trace validation. Slice path should be `tau traycer validate` for one trace/handoff, then `tau traycer chain-validate` for ordered handoff/monitor receipts as a degenerate DAG, then `tau traycer dag-validate` over an explicit `tau.dag_contract.v1` with branches and joins. DAG validation should consume per-agent `tau.monitor_receipt.v1` artifacts and final handoffs, enforce shared goal hash and target, allowed nodes/edges, required nodes, required joins after dependencies, DAG-level evidence coverage, no hidden unresolved REVIEW/REROUTE/BLOCK alerts, and final handoff references to the DAG monitor receipt. DAG drift is an orchestrator concern: per-agent monitors detect local drift, while DAG Traycer detects graph drift such as unexpected nodes/edges, missing reviewer/join nodes, goal or target divergence, scope collisions, orphan artifacts, conflicting claims, and cycles.

## Recent Decisions

| Date | Decision | Why |
|------|----------|-----|
| 2026-07-05 | Blocked subagents must report blockers and stop test-only drift before further retries | Agents often hide blockers by running non-essential deterministic unit tests. Tau now treats test-only churn without task evidence as `pointless_unit_test_drift`, requires a blocker report in `tau.course_correction.v1`, and requires `$brave-search` before a third local attempt after two failures. |
| 2026-07-04 | Adaptive DAG features must carry proof through every implemented branch before reporting remaining non-claims | The `dag-route-memory-sync --apply` branch was implemented but initially only dry-run/proof-collection tested. Tau now has live Memory apply/readback receipts for both proof and production collections, and future adaptive DAG work should continue into any deterministically testable implemented branch rather than stopping at caveats. |
| 2026-06-27 | Initialize project knowledge | Enable shared human/agent context |
| 2026-06-27 | Use a fork at grahama1970/tau rather than a new unrelated repo | The project already has upstream history at alejandro-ao/tau, so a fork preserves attribution and makes future upstream comparison/pull possible. |
| 2026-06-27 | Keep GitHub mutation out of the first harness slices | Current proof is schema, validator, fixture, and deterministic projection only; live issue creation should come after the contracts are accepted. |
| 2026-06-27 | Keep registry command dispatch opt-in per agent | A real agent registry can contain many roles, but Tau should only execute commands for entries with explicit `tau-dispatch-command.json`. Missing specs fail closed with a `BLOCKED` receipt. |
| 2026-06-27 | Store experimental dispatch command specs in Tau overlays | This avoids depending on untracked files in the dirty `agent-skills` repo while still proving routes against real registry identities. |
| 2026-06-27 | Treat `goal-guardian` as a Tau built-in dispatch role | It is a protocol guard rather than a current `agent-skills/agents` directory entry, so the overlay loader allows built-in Tau roles while still requiring external registry entries for non-built-in agents. |
| 2026-06-27 | Prove multi-step command loops before GitHub mutation | Local command-loop receipts provide stronger evidence for route continuity than isolated one-step receipts while still avoiding durable GitHub writes. |
| 2026-06-27 | Require dry-run terminal GitHub transport before live GitHub writes | The command-loop terminal projection must render exact comment and label commands before any future `--apply` path is considered. |
| 2026-06-27 | Keep live GitHub writes behind an explicit `--apply` flag | Default command-loop GitHub transport remains dry-run; `--apply` is only allowed after the terminal command-loop receipt validates and stops at `human`. |
| 2026-06-27 | Require GitHub auth and target preflight before command-loop mutation | A valid receipt alone is not enough for live writes; Tau must prove the local `gh` session and target issue/PR are available before comment or label commands run. |
| 2026-06-27 | Make Memory pipeline stages receipt-backed | Sparta Chat/TUI should render `Getting Intent...`, `Extracting Entities...`, `Accessing Memory...`, and branch-specific labels from harness receipts, not from hidden reasoning text or UI-only theater. |
| 2026-06-27 | Version the UX Lab Tau chat surface with receipt-backed stage rendering | `#tau` was already referenced by UX Lab routing, but the Tau chat files were untracked in pi-mono. Committing them makes the route reproducible and ties visible process status to `tau.loop2_pipeline_stage.v1` metadata. |
| 2026-06-27 | Treat live composer stage capture as a separate proof rung | Static receipt panels do not prove dynamic chat behavior. The next UI rungs should keep saving screenshots and summaries for actual submitted turns. |
| 2026-06-27 | Do not emit subagent/GitHub handoff metadata from failed Memory route products | `/intent` success alone is not enough to route downstream. If `/clarify`, `/deflect`, or `/answer` fails, Tau should expose the failed stage and stop before fabricating a Memory product or agent handoff. |
| 2026-06-27 | Do not fake an ANSWER browser route when Memory intent does not select it | The live answer endpoint is separate evidence from browser route selection. A future Tau slice can add an explicit answer route fixture or improve intent coverage, but current live UI proof should report the limitation honestly. |
| 2026-06-27 | Render handoff JSON from Tau-owned adapter content instead of a shared-chat-only panel | The shared chat file has unrelated local edits, so the safer bounded slice is to emit the JSON contract from `TauReceiptAdapter` message content and verify it through the existing renderer. |
| 2026-06-27 | Add a reviewer overlay before claiming UI handoffs are executable | The Tau chat handoff routes successful compliance turns to `reviewer`; the harness needed an explicit bounded reviewer command spec before a UI-extracted handoff could enter `handoff-command-loop`. |
| 2026-06-27 | Treat UI-originated `target: "new"` terminal handoffs as dry-run issue creation | The live Tau chat handoff is not attached to an existing issue yet. Terminal GitHub transport should derive a ticket-create projection rather than requiring an existing issue/PR target. |
| 2026-06-27 | Use direct `$webgpt` for Tau phase/architecture escalation | `$ask` added avoidable browser-bundle friction for Tau in this workflow; direct `$webgpt -p tau` produced the create-architecture solution bundle and kept WebGPT output as design input rather than closure proof. |
| 2026-06-27 | Bridge human goal changes into the existing handoff loop instead of adding a parallel loop | The smallest useful feature is a deterministic conversion from human-only goal-change packets to a normal `goal-guardian` start handoff, keeping the existing validator/dispatch/receipt path in control. |
| 2026-06-27 | Stop human goal changes at goal-guardian until a human goal decision exists | A bridged goal change must not be treated as ordinary preserved-goal PASS. Goal-guardian now emits a reconciliation receipt and routes to `human` rather than continuing to verifier/worker roles. |
| 2026-06-27 | Keep ticket reconciliation source explicit and local for the first classification slice | Goal-guardian can classify a structured `tau.goal_guardian_ticket_source.v1` artifact without requiring live GitHub mutation or hidden issue discovery. |
| 2026-06-27 | Project reconciliation receipts to GitHub before live mutation | Classified goal-guardian output now has an inspectable `gh issue comment/edit` dry-run projection; live writes still require `--apply` plus existing auth/target preflight. |
| 2026-06-27 | Fetch GitHub ticket sources through an explicit read-only command | Goal-guardian needs real GitHub-shaped tickets, but Tau should not mutate GitHub or fabricate ticket state. The fetch command is dry-run by default and `--execute` only runs `gh issue list`. |
| 2026-06-27 | Prefer explicit goal-guardian ticket-source inputs over hidden env state | The adapter can now classify a passed `--ticket-source` even when the fallback env var is absent or wrong, making receipts easier to reproduce from command artifacts. |
| 2026-06-27 | Record explicit ticket-source inputs in command-loop receipts | Passing `--goal-guardian-ticket-source` appends the source path to the goal-guardian adapter command, which makes the receipt replayable from command artifacts rather than out-of-band environment setup. |
| 2026-06-27 | Project command-loop reconciliation through GitHub with source trace | The wrapper command avoids manually locating the reconciliation artifact and records loop, reconciliation, and ticket-source paths next to the dry-run GitHub commands. |
| 2026-06-27 | Rewrite README using the Watch README shape | Tau needs a human-facing project overview, not only an inherited teaching-project README. The new README starts from the visible product promise, then explains the harness, Memory-first chat direction, and proof boundaries. |
| 2026-06-27 | Compress the Tâ€™au header image with Pillow into WebP | The current source PNG `/home/graham/Downloads/ChatGPT Image Jun 27, 2026, 07_58_56 PM.png` was 2,559,239 bytes at 1672x941. `docs/assets/tau-header.webp` is 175,472 bytes at 1600x900, which keeps the README visual lightweight. |
| 2026-06-27 | Make Tâ€™au the owner of the chat UX contract | UX Lab should host/reference Tâ€™au like Watch does, not become the canonical source of the Tâ€™au chat UX. The contract lives at `ui/tau-chat-contract.json` and marks UX Lab as `integration_viewer`. |
| 2026-06-27 | Expand README around loop, harness, TUI, chat, and upstream delta | The README previously described the harness direction but did not clearly explain the four surfaces or what changed from upstream Tau. |
| 2026-06-27 | Add current TUI and React chat screenshots to README | The README should show the real terminal and browser surfaces because the original upstream Tau had limited rendering. The screenshots must remain proof-scoped as rendering evidence only. |
| 2026-06-27 | Add Tau-owned Docker Compose stack | The project needs a simple Docker entrypoint like Watch. Tau owns the CLI/cron containers; cross-project services remain external and explicit rather than silently vendored into this repo. |
| 2026-06-27 | Merge Kimi README prose without dropping architecture sections | Kimi's prose improved the top-level explanation, but its draft omitted the newer ownership-boundary details, so only the clearer opening and phrasing were adopted. |
| 2026-06-28 | Keep special orchestrated subagent mode explicit | The cron/GitHub-ticket loop is activated only by `--start` or `TAU_ORCHESTRATOR_START`; ordinary Tâ€™au chat/CLI turns must not be described as autonomous ticket loops. |
